  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c4355991-c333-431b-bd32-67f094fff4dd'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">In a country named Panem, every year 12-18 year olds are chosen and put in an arena. They have try and survive for their life while the others try to <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">In a country named Panem, every year 12-18 year olds are chosen and put in an arena. They have try and survive for their life while the others try to defeat them. Only one person could be made victor. The story revolves around a girl named Katniss. Her sister gets chosen for the arena but Katniss volunteers to take her place.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15304597352067800888"><u>3 A game of Life and Death ★'s</u> <br/><br/><b>
  <i>“This is a girl who starts a revolution. This is a girl who changes the world!”</i>
</b> ―<i>Jennifer Lawrence</i> <br/><br/>I absolutely love <i>The Hunger Games</i> books and the movies were brilliantly done! Phenomenal!!! (Think I may have to do a reread soon). I have seen all 4 movies over a dozen times... seriously no joke. I really liked getting a <i>"behind-the-scenes"</i> look at <i>The Hunger Games movie</i>! I enjoyed all of the information, the pictures, the actors/actresses thoughts and the step</span>
  <span id="freeText15304597352067800888" style="display:none"><u>3 A game of Life and Death ★'s</u> <br><br><b>
  <i>“This is a girl who starts a revolution. This is a girl who changes the world!”</i>
</b> ―<i>Jennifer Lawrence</i> <br><br>I absolutely love <i>The Hunger Games</i> books and the movies were brilliantly done! Phenomenal!!! (Think I may have to do a reread soon). I have seen all 4 movies over a dozen times... seriously no joke. I really liked getting a <i>"behind-the-scenes"</i> look at <i>The Hunger Games movie</i>! I enjoyed all of the information, the pictures, the actors/actresses thoughts and the step by step of what all went into it. It had all the information I wanted to know about the director, what parts <i>Suzanne Collins</i> was involved in, the casting, etc... It was a quick easy read, all of the photos and illustrations were all so great. This would make a great addition for any <i>Hunger Games</i> fans collection. <br><br><b>Rebellion. Revenge. Tragic loss.</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1564794734i/27931312.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="15304597352067800888" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_280672518" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/280672518" />
    <a title="Penelope" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/675363-penelope"><img alt="Penelope" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568151251p2/675363.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/280672518?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Penelope" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Penelope" href="/user/show/675363-penelope">Penelope</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/675363-penelope?shelf=reviewed-books">reviewed-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer280672518" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15579624675972110850"><blockquote><i>"...I think a book adaptation doesn't have to be just like the book, it has to feel like the book. That's what you want. You want to get the feeling from the movie that you got from the book, and you want the characters to evoke the characters that you fell in love with."</i><br/>-Nina Jacobson (producer), pg. 20</blockquote><br/><br/>I can't even begin to describe how many worries and fears about the making of the movie, this book put to rest. Just reading about the careful decisions that were made through every step of the p</span>
  <span id="freeText15579624675972110850" style="display:none"><blockquote><i>"...I think a book adaptation doesn't have to be just like the book, it has to feel like the book. That's what you want. You want to get the feeling from the movie that you got from the book, and you want the characters to evoke the characters that you fell in love with."</i><br />-Nina Jacobson (producer), pg. 20</blockquote><br /><br />I can't even begin to describe how many worries and fears about the making of the movie, this book put to rest. Just reading about the careful decisions that were made through every step of the process, and about exactly how much each person involved cares about keeping the integrity of the series, was well worth the cost of this book. Reasons for why certain elements of the book were changed for the movie are explained in a way that make me feel very confident that those in charge have the reader's/viewer's best interests at heart.<br /><br />Just reading quotes from Gary Ross (the director) talking about Katniss, made me smile. I can tell that he truly *gets* Katniss; that he understands her enough to portray her story in a true and faithful adaptation. For me, that's what is important. I chose that quote at the top there, because I agree with it wholeheartedly; I can deal with different hair color, missing characters, and other changes...as long as the characters are the same ones I fell in love with, and as long as the movie makes me feel that same powerful way that the book did.<br /><br />*Clears throat* Moving on....It was nice getting to see how things work behind the scenes. For someone who doesn't know a lot about what goes into making a movie, I appreciate the fact that each step of the process is explained; from Suzanne Collins' experience with getting the book published, to why the production company/director/cast was chosen, the thought that went into the costumes, the food, and the locations, and all the way to what it was like on set. I loved learning all these things I didn't know before. There is a wealth of information that did not allow me to put the book down. Each time I tried, I learned something new and interesting.<br /><br /><blockquote><i>"The book--and now the film--captures themes and concerns that seem timely.<br />But its real strength, in the end, is that it's timeless. It speaks to us today, and it will speak--even more powerfully--tomorrow."</i><br />-Kate Egan, pg. 154</blockquote><br /><br />As far as pictures, the companion includes a large amount of brand new pics of the cast, the set, early digital renderings of scenes, and various pics behind-the-scenes, along with some pics that have been around for a while. Although some have recently been released in various places online, there are still many pics hat I have yet to see anywhere but in this companion.<br /><br />The only drawback I can see, is that I felt like maybe this was a bit too much information for me...at least right now. I'm one who likes to be completely surprised in a movie, and so the less I know going in, the better. But now I know SO many things about the movie, that I'm hoping I won't be concentrating on recognizing the details this companion mentions, instead of just enjoying the movie.<br /><br />Overall, I think this is a strong movie companion, and definitely something you will want to add to your collection. This book put my fears about the movie to rest, and secured my trust that no one else on Earth could have been involved, who would have been more true to the series. It pumped me up, and made me extremely excited for the movie (didn't think I could get more excited, did ya?). And it will do the same to you.<br /><br /><br />This review was originally published on my blog. <b>See the full review at: <a href="http://www.thereadingfever.com/2012/03/book-review-hunger-games-official.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Reading Fever</a>.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="15579624675972110850" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_496431536" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/496431536" />
    <a title="Stephanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9998105-stephanie"><img alt="Stephanie" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/496431536?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephanie" href="/user/show/9998105-stephanie">Stephanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9998105-stephanie?shelf=dystopia">dystopia</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9998105-stephanie?shelf=kick-ass-heroines">kick-ass-heroines</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer496431536" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5728826332858188329">For fans of The Hunger Games, particularly those with an interest in film-making, this book is immensely satisfying. I've read many articles on the upcoming movie, and I was happy to see that most of the photos, if not all, have not been previously published. Quotes were included from all of the actors, as well the producers, director, and various crew.<br/><br/>The book includes six parts:<br/><br/>Part 1: "The History of The Hunger Games" details the film industry's immediate interest following the publication of</span>
  <span id="freeText5728826332858188329" style="display:none">For fans of The Hunger Games, particularly those with an interest in film-making, this book is immensely satisfying. I've read many articles on the upcoming movie, and I was happy to see that most of the photos, if not all, have not been previously published. Quotes were included from all of the actors, as well the producers, director, and various crew.<br /><br />The book includes six parts:<br /><br />Part 1: "The History of The Hunger Games" details the film industry's immediate interest following the publication of the book, Suzanne Collins's selection of a producer for the film, and the hiring of Gary Ross as director.<br /><br />Part 2: "The Cast of The Hunger Games" focuses heavily on the casting of Jennifer Lawrence and Josh Hutcherson as Katniss and Peeta. The book also, ahem, pays tribute to the actors playing the other main tributes, as well as to the casting of major Capitol characters including Cinna, Effie, and President Snow.<br /><br />Part 3: "The Look of The Hunger Games: Places and Props" details the areas in North Carolina used in the film and has many photos of various sets in District 12, the Arena, and the Capitol. One of the photos shows all of the tributes seated in the hovercraft, on the way to the Arena, and another shows the construction of the cornucopia.<br /><br />Part 4: "The Look of The Hunger Games: People" shows Capitol residents in their garish clothing and makeup, along with the much more subdued residents of District 12. This section has photos of perhaps all of Katniss's outfits and costumes, from her drab District 12 duds to her "Girl on Fire" dress.<br /><br />Part 5: "The Filming of The Hunger Games" details the challenges of filming in the summer heat and rain in the North Carolina forest. Particular attention is paid to the fireball scene.<br /><br />Part 6: "The Legacy of The Hunger Games" sets the stage for the filming of the sequel, "Catching Fire."</span>
  <a data-text-id="5728826332858188329" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_311320344" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/311320344" />
    <a title="Jennifer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3956348-jennifer"><img alt="Jennifer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1329444637p2/3956348.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/311320344?book_show_action=true">Apr 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer" href="/user/show/3956348-jennifer">Jennifer</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer311320344" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13785875399816633241">4.5/5 stars<br/><br/>If you've seen the movie and love the book then this is a nice companion to the Hunger Games movie.<br/><br/>The Illustrated Movie Companion has lots of pictures and is divided into sections. They focus on the book, the casting, the places, the costumes and more.<br/><br/>As someone who loved the books and enjoyed the movie it was nice to see how everything transpired.<br/><br/>I especially loved hearing about Suzanne Collins (the author of the series) and things that happened with the Hunger Games book (and her i</span>
  <span id="freeText13785875399816633241" style="display:none">4.5/5 stars<br /><br />If you've seen the movie and love the book then this is a nice companion to the Hunger Games movie.<br /><br />The Illustrated Movie Companion has lots of pictures and is divided into sections. They focus on the book, the casting, the places, the costumes and more.<br /><br />As someone who loved the books and enjoyed the movie it was nice to see how everything transpired.<br /><br />I especially loved hearing about Suzanne Collins (the author of the series) and things that happened with the Hunger Games book (and her involvement with the movie).<br /><br />I loved hearing info about the Hunger Games book. For example the original title for the first book was, The Tribute of District Twelve. And the Hunger Games was originally going to be 3rd person in the past tense.<br /><br />I really enjoyed reading about the casting. Although instead of just focusing on the cast they chose and why they were perfect for the roles i would have liked to read about the process of who was in the running for each role and ultimately why they were/weren't chosen (but I do understand why they just focused on those cast). I just think as a reader it would have been fascinating.<br /><br />Overall, this Movie Companion was a fun read. And if you are a fan of the movie then it is definitely a must read.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13785875399816633241" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer779203104362666079">Since I really enjoyed the Hunger Games books, I've naturally been excited for the upcoming movie.   <span id="freeText779203104362666079" style="display:none">Since I really enjoyed the Hunger Games books, I've naturally been excited for the upcoming movie. My mama surprised me by giving me this movie companion and, while it was an easy read, all of the photographs and illustrations were incredible. This is going to be a visually stunning movie; from the food, to the set of the area, to the fashions and makeup of the Capitol. <br /><br />Even though I'm not yet sure that I'll be seeing the film in March when it comes out, the book was well-worth the read to not only give me a peek into the making of the Hunger Games film, but also fuel my love and interest in the general movie-making process.</span>

    <a title="Sanara♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28883553-sanara"><img alt="Sanara♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514550998p2/28883553.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<div id="review_274669635" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/274669635" />
    <a title="Holly Noelle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4189131-holly-noelle"><img alt="Holly Noelle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1286852224p2/4189131.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/274669635?book_show_action=true">Feb 08, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Holly Noelle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Holly Noelle" href="/user/show/4189131-holly-noelle">Holly Noelle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Hunger Games movie and book fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4189131-holly-noelle?shelf=books-to-movies">books-to-movies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4189131-holly-noelle?shelf=reading-challenge-2012">reading-challenge-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4189131-holly-noelle?shelf=in-my-library">in-my-library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer274669635" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12324211380940119238">More like a 3.5.<br/><br/>I enjoyed reading this. Unlike the other tribute guide (Ugh) I was pleased by how this was written. This was interesting, and gave me insight to the behind the scenes aspects of the film.<br/><br/>The interviews with Gary Ross and Nina Jacobson were precisely why I wanted to read it. I wanted to know why they chose to deviate from the books and why they went in certain directions. It threw me when Lenny Kravitz and Josh Hutcherson were cast, but I feel like this gives the audience a better</span>
  <span id="freeText12324211380940119238" style="display:none">More like a 3.5.<br /><br />I enjoyed reading this. Unlike the other tribute guide (Ugh) I was pleased by how this was written. This was interesting, and gave me insight to the behind the scenes aspects of the film.<br /><br />The interviews with Gary Ross and Nina Jacobson were precisely why I wanted to read it. I wanted to know why they chose to deviate from the books and why they went in certain directions. It threw me when Lenny Kravitz and Josh Hutcherson were cast, but I feel like this gives the audience a better idea. I may not agree with the choices, but I understand it. They alerted everyone to the malicious President Snow whereas the books foreshadow more than anything. Yet, their choices make sense cinematically.<br /><br />Furthermore, this book drives home the fact that people behind the scenes were essentially obsessed with doing this right. They wanted the film to reflect and portray what we read in the books. They wanted the fans to be happy. Looking to the past to create the future? Wanting the capitol to look avant-garde, and completely unattainable, to the audience? Wanting the cast members physically doing the stunt work? This makes me a fan of the movie all the more. <br /><br />Loved the interviews with the cast. The characters of Cato, Clove, Glimmer, foxface, and Rue gave great information about the filming process. Learning about how they were selected makes me appreciate them. Stoked Isabelle Fuhrman is such a fan of the series and I adore Amandla Stenberg. Her audition story made me laugh.<br /><br />While I enjoyed the pictures I would have preferred more shooting shots. I did like the art work, but I think seeing more things actually being filmed would have made this book better. Plus, I think there was a lot of focus on Jack Quaid (Marvel) who wasn't a huge fixture in the movie. I get his parents are famous, but I would have preferred more information on Dayo Okeniyi (Thresh) who had a more significant role.<br /><br />I also wanted elaboration on other choices. They mentioned the District 11 bread but not why the cut it. Suzanne Collins said she chose to eliminate Madge, but not why. These key elements differed from screen to movie and while the movie still proved entertaining, I would like to know why they changed those in the script.<br /><br />I recommend it to all fans of the books and movie. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12324211380940119238" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_231388125" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Gabriella" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4006319-gabriella"><img alt="Gabriella" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1287296249p2/4006319.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/231388125?book_show_action=true">Nov 05, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gabriella" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gabriella" href="/user/show/4006319-gabriella">Gabriella</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer231388125" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14060489944973327550">I am one of those crazy people/obsessive fans that has a meltdown everytime it is announced that one of my favourite books is going to be made into a movie. Indeed after I found out that The Hunger Games movie is not just a rumour but is actually happening... well lets just say you wouldn't have wanted to be sharing brain space with me at that exact moment.<br/><br/>So for months and months all these scenarios have been running through my head on why I am not going to like this movie.<br/>* The actors won't ma</span>
  <span id="freeText14060489944973327550" style="display:none">I am one of those crazy people/obsessive fans that has a meltdown everytime it is announced that one of my favourite books is going to be made into a movie. Indeed after I found out that The Hunger Games movie is not just a rumour but is actually happening... well lets just say you wouldn't have wanted to be sharing brain space with me at that exact moment.<br /><br />So for months and months all these scenarios have been running through my head on why I am not going to like this movie.<br />* The actors won't match the characters<br />* Vital scenes are going to get cut from the script<br />* Small details are going to get cut, which will make the movie lose some of the books original magic.<br /><br />And I really didn't think my fears were unfounded. After seeing other book to movie conversions that were epic epic fails, I was seriously praying for a miracle. (Eg. of epic epic fails: Twilight series, parts of the Harry Potter series - but especially movie #5, &amp; the True Blood TV series [Sookie Stackhouse])<br /><br />So when THG: Official Illustrated Movie Companion released I was eager to get my hands on it. But only because it was about the Hunger Games. I had no idea that it was all about the production of the film and how it all started. Obviously I don't pay too close attention to book titles.<br /><br />I am so glad I read THG: Official Illustrated Movie Companion. It actually took away all my fears and insecurities for the coming movie. This book proved to me that it is going to be made by the very best. All the people working on The Hunger Games movies creation have put a lot of thought and effort into ALL aspects of the movie, from the actors to the sets, to the overall essence of just what the hunger games are. And I must say that it was a massive relief for me to read that Suzanne Collins played a large part in the writing of the script.<br /><br />THG: Official Illustrated Movie Companion has finally made me excited to see the movie.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14060489944973327550" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7173714262916838146"><blockquote>
  <i>"This is a girl who starts a revolution. This is a girl who changes the world."</i>
</blockquote><br/>I feel like reading <i>The Hunger Games</i> and watching <i>The Hunger Games</i> movies all over again in order to re-live my experiences and emotions while reading and watching <i>The Hunger Games</i>. <b>The nostalgia is real!</b><br/><br/>This movie companion reads like a magazine. It's full of stunning graphics, pull-out quotes and vibrant colours which makes it easy to browse through and enjoy.<br/><br/><i>The Hunger Games:Official Illustrated Movie Companion</i></span>
  <span id="freeText7173714262916838146" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"This is a girl who starts a revolution. This is a girl who changes the world."</i>
</blockquote><br />I feel like reading <i>The Hunger Games</i> and watching <i>The Hunger Games</i> movies all over again in order to re-live my experiences and emotions while reading and watching <i>The Hunger Games</i>. <b>The nostalgia is real!</b><br /><br />This movie companion reads like a magazine. It's full of stunning graphics, pull-out quotes and vibrant colours which makes it easy to browse through and enjoy.<br /><br /><i>The Hunger Games:Official Illustrated Movie Companion</i> made me understand and appreciate the effort that went into creating the <i>Hunger Games</i> movies. All the people who worked to create the <i>Hunger Games</i> movies, from the director, to the cast and designers, had a <b>passion and love for the original work,wanted to draw inspiration from it and give it the respect that it deserves</b>. Many of <i>The Hunger Games</i> movie-making secrets are revealed. I learnt about the extra attention to detail that was paid to every single thing, such as the food and style, and admired the happiness, friendship and family-nature of the team. <b>That's definitely AMAZING!</b><br /><br /><i>The Hunger Games:Official Illustrated Movie Companion</i> not only gave me an insider view into the process of making a movie, but it also made me <b>appreciate the <i>Hunger Games</i> movies and the team that brought it to life</b>. Definitely recommend it for fans of <i>The Hunger Games</i><br /><blockquote>
  <i>"In future films, this mockingjay will soar."</i>
</blockquote></span>

  <span id="freeText14728901170351825853" style="display:none">I enjoy reading about all that went into making the movies. I didn't read it before the movie because I really didn't want a lot of spoilers. I liked the parts in which Suzanne Collins is quoted the best. Since it is the author's story I like to hear what the author has to say the most. i.e.<br /><br />"If Josh had been bright purple and had had six foot wings and have that audition, I'd have been like 'Cast him! We an work around the wings!' He was that good." <br /><br />and her thoughts about what she wants people - especially young people - to get out of the books.<br /><br />"It's crucial that young readers are considering scenarios about humanity's future, because the challenges are about to land in their laps. I hope they question how elements of the book might be relevant in their own lives. About global warming, about our mistreatment of the environment, but also questions like: How do you feel about the fact that she people take their next meal for granted when so many other people are starving in the world? What do you think about choices your government, past and present, or other governments around the world make? What's your relationship to reality TV versus your relationship to the news? Was there any thing in the book that disturbed you because it reflected aspects of your own life, and if there was, what can you do about it? Because you know what? Even if they're not of your making, these issues and how to deal with them will become your responsibility."</span>

<div id="review_1105045825" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1105045825" />
    <a title="Sharon Powers" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30801573-sharon-powers"><img alt="Sharon Powers" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1431988633p2/30801573.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1105045825?book_show_action=true">Nov 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sharon Powers" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sharon Powers" href="/user/show/30801573-sharon-powers">Sharon Powers</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1105045825" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6517727012488193261">Book Review by Sharon Powers.<br/><br/>QUICK BOOK REVIEW OF THE OFFICIAL ILLUSTRATED MOVIE COMPANION<br/> (THE HUNGER GAMES).<br/><br/>The Hunger Games: Official Illustrated<br/>Movie Companion, by Kate Egan is 160 pages;<br/>it sells for $9.99 to about $18.99, of course,<br/>depending on where you buy your book.<br/>[15]<br/> The Movie Companion is divided into six parts, as follows:<br/>(1) The History of The Hunger Games;<br/>(2) The Cast of The Hunger Games;<br/>(3) The Look of The Hunger Games: Places and Props;<br/>(4) The Look of The Hunger Games: People;<br/>(5</span>
  <span id="freeText6517727012488193261" style="display:none">Book Review by Sharon Powers.<br /><br />QUICK BOOK REVIEW OF THE OFFICIAL ILLUSTRATED MOVIE COMPANION<br /> (THE HUNGER GAMES).<br /><br />The Hunger Games: Official Illustrated<br />Movie Companion, by Kate Egan is 160 pages;<br />it sells for $9.99 to about $18.99, of course,<br />depending on where you buy your book.<br />[15]<br /> The Movie Companion is divided into six parts, as follows:<br />(1) The History of The Hunger Games;<br />(2) The Cast of The Hunger Games;<br />(3) The Look of The Hunger Games: Places and Props;<br />(4) The Look of The Hunger Games: People;<br />(5) The Filming of The Hunger Games; and,<br />(6) The Legacy of The Hunger Games.<br /><br /> The first section on the history of The Hunger Games covers the history of Hunger Games. It also deals with violence and the "challenge of how to present the violence while still maintaining a PG-13 rating" so the intended audience can view the movie (as well as read the book). (p.14) [15] I found this section very interesting and of great interest in examining how the violence was handled in the book and movie.<br /><br /><br />One page showing beautiful glossy photographs of actors,<br />Woody Harrelson, as Haymitch, and Lenny Kravitz, as Cinna.<br /> Obviously, one of the big draws of the book is to talk about the major stars of the film. This section discusses how actors were selected, gives us comments from the actors, views of the director, producers, and others, and shows us amazing glossy, beautiful photographs of the actors.<br /><br /> Section three is an extensive section that relates concepts like how locations portray "power and might and authority" (p.49) or how a forest area was selected because it had hardwood trees instead of coniferous trees, to convey the feeling of a "uniquely American" location. (p.59) Also, considerations of colors, for example, the Capitol, food and clothes, to be vibrant in "Blues, oranges, greens...but not any pastels, not any earth tones, Nothing brown." (p.81) This is a huge section of the book that covers a lot of material, and the importance of some themes in the movie--like food. Everything from how several pigs were roasted and how the apple was placed in its mouth for Katniss to shoot, to the importance of bread and the types of different rolls, their color, and symbolism.<br /><br /> Section Four, not only shows photographs of the costumes of the actors, but actually goes into how the "look of the characters," came about. (p.88) Makeup artists, colorists, and costume designers had their work cut out for them.<br /><br /> Personally, I found Section Five to be the most interesting section in the book. The author states that one of the very most important things about adapting the book into a movie is "to convey the immediacy, the first-person point of view that the book has." The author, Kate Egan, explains that in adapting the book to the movie, they wanted to make sure that wherever possible, they kept Katniss Everdeen's point of view--as did the book! (p. 138)<br /><br /> The final section, although the shortest, covers some of the most important material. The author speaks to the timeliness of the book's/movie's themes, and Director Gary Ross explains how people were manipulated into participation in The Hunger Games. He says that by getting people involved in that horrendous contest, they become invested in the contestants. They begin "rooting for their favorites,"<br />which is more effective than attempting to subjugate them. The end result is people participate "in our system." (p.154).<br /><br /><br />One page from Kate Egan's book shows the beginning<br />of a scene. This is pages 66 &amp; 67 in the book. This scene<br />shows Peeta and Katniss (actors Jennifer Lawrence and<br />Josh Hutcherson.). Thank you to my husband, Carl, for<br />holding the book for me while I took the picture.<br /> Reiterating part of Section Five, the author, again, speaks to the importance of addressing controversial themes, but takes that notion a step further, addressing the importance of readers questioning the relevance of elements of books in their own lives. I agree with this idea and have addressed this concept in other blog posts. Books are so very important and can expand a person's thinking and reasoning skills if the reader asks pertinent questions about the book.<br /><br />CONCLUSION OF MOVIE GUIDE:<br /><br />[16]<br /> I really enjoyed this movie companion to The Hunger Games. The background information on the actors was fun, but more important was how the book was adapted to fit the big screen and still keep the integrity of the book. It is always a dicey thing to adapt a book to another media, such as big screen, so I enjoyed looking at how the movie makers approached this huge task. I also really enjoyed the discussions about the controversial themes, and how the author and movie makers addressed this big problem. I give this guide 4.0 stars out of 5.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6517727012488193261" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1582374889" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1582374889" />
    <a title="Madeline" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47978501-madeline"><img alt="Madeline" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1445355970p2/47978501.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1582374889?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Madeline" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Madeline" href="/user/show/47978501-madeline">Madeline</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1582374889" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17661650978445881790">Madeline Janus <br/>3/17/16 <br/>Period ⅘ <br/><br/> The book I read was “The Hunger Games”. It is the official illustrated movie companion. This book told you about how they made the movie. How they filmed, produced, and got creative ideas. This book told you about the characters and recent jobs they did before the started casting “The Hunger Games”. Also it told you how the characters acted with each other on and off set. The book also shows pictures. The pictures are off things on and off set. It showed you how </span>
  <span id="freeText17661650978445881790" style="display:none">Madeline Janus <br />3/17/16 <br />Period ⅘ <br /><br /> The book I read was “The Hunger Games”. It is the official illustrated movie companion. This book told you about how they made the movie. How they filmed, produced, and got creative ideas. This book told you about the characters and recent jobs they did before the started casting “The Hunger Games”. Also it told you how the characters acted with each other on and off set. The book also shows pictures. The pictures are off things on and off set. It showed you how they got ready. It showed how Catniss Everdeen did her hair. Also how Peta painted himself for the tree seen during the game. They showed the pictures of most of the characters outfits and them in them. Also it showed how they made the set. How they made all the props where Catniss goes and shoots the arrow in President Snows apple. <br /> I really liked this book. I thought it was really cool how they made the props. They had to spend hours making them and that shows hard work. I really like how all the characters got along on and off set. That shows team work. Hard work is a good lesson to learn same with team work. It really showed how they all worked together and got through it. I think this book does teach you good skills and makes you think and use your imagination. This book would be really good for people who are into the arts. It really lets you use your imagination and think outside of the box.<br /> I think this book was a little confusing at times. Even though it was a picture book it had confusing wording, from my point of view. The book does a lot of justice to the movie. The book did make it seem better than ever and made you want to keep reading. If they were to ever make another book on how they made the other “Hunger Game” movies I would definitely read it! All in all I thought this was a really outstanding book and recommend it to many people. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17661650978445881790" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SY8uymBdJbAdpRg1XXGmEe5w7TT08NEGlX9h1DtJrMLp5AHN9WC2G/l+aAT5orCb3j3XFIK9W5uTCCDz6vPdvw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('491BBID40fD4iCudjBlG5rJUDUZt20cZ1qoZGBwkfNhDtm4DFcVCWxxTW6woylBsghk3ZhuWzYTQ3Vg/zZ4NpQ==')})
  }

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/16692130-the-hunger-games-official-illustrated-movie-companion">Quotes from The Hunger Games:...</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">

            <span class="readable">&ldquo;In The Hunger Games, there's something for everyone. <br /> A gripping adventure.<br /> A political commentary.<br /> A love story.<br /> A cautionary tale.<br />Some call it science fiction, some call it potential reality.<br />Some say it's for teenagers, some say it's for adults.<br />The book--and now the film--captures themes and concerns that seem timely.<br />But its real strength, in the end, is that it's timeless. It speaks to us today, and it will speak--even more powerfully--tomorrow.&rdquo;</span>
            <nobr>
              &mdash;
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/quotes/505783-in-the-hunger-games-there-s-something-for-everyone-a-gripping">10 likes</a>

          </div>
          <div class="stacked" tyle="padding-bottom:15px">
            <span class="readable">&ldquo;I felt that Lionsgate really understood the material and that they would let us make a faithful adaptation; that they wouldn't soften it, they wouldn't age up the characters, to make them older so that it would be more palatable. I felt that the power of the book was in the youth of these protagonists and that you couldn't cheat on that in terms of their age in the story. Lionsgate was on board for, of course, the PG-13 version of the movie, not something full of blood and guts, but something more thematically driven. -Nina Jacobson, pg. 14&rdquo;</span>
